Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and we who are in our time, place a poultice on it with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the magnet cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", by which it is shaped:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then perforate the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then insert alum, as we have said; and when the work is completed prepare the patient's bed in a dark place, where he sleeps on his back in darkness; and be careful of all movements, and give him light food, and let him not move his head to either side, and keep him tied according to his disposition until the third day; then release him from this same dark house, examine his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is necessary that you do this slowly, because the eye becomes inflamed quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess appears, instruct the patient to unbind the eye in front on the seventh day, and the dressing that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then loosen the eye bandage and place a layer of earth over its face for one day, and be thus in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then run from the dark house and return to your own place, and know that no disciples should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach (a region in medieval Europe), who told us that in their land they did make a magnet instrument, which pierced through water, but somehow I never saw any of them in our land, nor did I ever read about it in old books; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of magnetite, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are of pure iron.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of them from this same subtlety, and the end in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the skin
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are sometimes born or newly formed wasps of various kinds, from which there are some that resemble scorpions by the multitude of their feet; and if they have a swollen body of fiery color, and if they have a smooth body of good colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	So then of these wasps that are smooth and not swollen, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the honey to those wasps, and drive them out; afterwards take what you can catch with the sharp end of a spatula on one side, as long as you know that the wasp is completely extracted.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cut out, then open it up to the full with the sharp instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without any swelling or festering sore, then clean the scort with what is needed; and if it's malignant swellings, then hasten and cauterize as much as is needed; and when the skin is stained and all the fat growths are cut out, then pour either hot oil or vinegar on them.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle works and moisture comes all the way up to the throat, you know that it is clean; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, you know that there is dry flesh in the bone above, to which instruments do not come to cut: then it is necessary that you put a piece of linen thread about a finger thick into the needle, and let it be knotted on hands so many, and have between each knot an interval of space about this much; and put the patient's head of the thread in his nape at its power, and draw it out smelling as long as it comes through the needle down into the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is a light thing for one who wants to do it; then take the head that comes through the needle with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other while they are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do so much as you know the hurt has corrupted that flesh, then take out the thread, wipe away the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that is left of flesh; and then put on a linen bandage some days until you are healed, and if there's need for dry medicines, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purify the head, at which we distill oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or lead, resembling an open lantern, like a jug, and guide it in the same way. And if you see [the thread], make a closed jug and let the instruments be full to purify the head; and have one handle at the top to hold when you heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the skin
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	The head of the skin often comes a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large in time, until it is visible to look at; and therefore you should cut it out at first, and remove all the dead flesh, then put on the place the cautery or the burning medicine. And if you delay cutting it out so long that it becomes large, be careful whether it is hard, with foul colour, with poor feeling: don't touch it with iron because it's an infected abscess, for when you cut it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of good appearance, not foul color, and you see that it can be cut out entirely, then empty the patient and the abscess with some fear and cure the place with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the skin has been cut and sewn back together
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuations of solution come in one of those cartilaginous works, it is a small thing to prevent it from happening, as has been seen in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to do as it happens in some cases, if you observe that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips with a suture, then care for it until it heals; and if the lips have already fallen apart on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their flesh as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, bind it, and powder on top bloodpowder of dragon, and incense broit; and put on top the powders a piece of plaster strong or another adhesive plaster, and let it be until it sets by itself, then care for it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is that you join the skin with:
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When people have hard abscesses inside their lips that look like grains of mustard seeds, small and large; then you must turn the lips back, split each one open, take it as a pair of scissors and clip it in each part; then apply vinegar on the area after making an incision until the sore is covered; and then sew the lip with linen, and cure the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is a piece of flesh stuck above the gums that they call "albulus"; if it needs to be taken out, you should grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root, and let it bleed or dry; then put vinegar on the area or other drying and desiccative powders; and if the flesh comes back after being cut, and many times happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it doesn't come back after the cautery, these are the ways of taking out growths.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, rough and ugly skin that is also hard to remove; and sometimes the tooth becomes black and yellowish and greenish with worms, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth smells bad. If this happens, you should make the sick person sit down between your hands, and take their hair in your sacred hand, and pull out the teeth or skin that appears, until there is nothing left; and do the same for all blackness, greenishness, yellowness, and other discolorations, until they are gone. And if you remove what is at the first cause, it's good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. Know that teeth need various forms of instruments to be pulled, according to what the work shows, because the extractor from which one removes teeth outside has different shapes than those from which one removes between teeth; and these forms and others should be at your disposal.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait a while before pulling it out as long as possible because it should not be done lightly; for this is a very high substance so there should be no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When then the patient is constrained to draw, it is necessary that you are certain of the vein's location.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain departs from the patient and they think it is in the good vein, and have the patient bleed from that vein; and nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad vein is extracted, for we have already shown this to be so with the same sainors; and when you are well certain of the location of the vein, then you must scrape around the vein at every point where it touches the gum very hard to protect the gums from all sides; then move it with your hands or fine pincers at first pace and pace, until they are well extracted, then firmly hold the pincers; and have the patient's head in your safe space between your knees, and keep them still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After you have extracted the vein properly without breaking it, and if it does not flow far, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and move it just like you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is pierced and gnawed, you must fill it with cloths, at the place where the hole is; and if you strain it gently with pincers, so that it does not break when straining it; and you must work very skillfully around the gum for to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and warn the patient that more severe pain will come from the root than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be warned that you do not act as ignorant surgeons who by their haste and boldness break the tooth at times, and do not bring about what we have mentioned; but often lead to severe illness through the roots that remain or from the tooth they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is loose, wash the area with vinegar or with plantain and sile; and if there is a discharge of blood which often happens, fill the area with vitriol powder; and if it does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, by which one must pull out teeth first, should be with long pointed tips and thick handles, so that they do not double back when you pull on the tooth; and these are the shapes.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have thick limbs that do not bend when pulled, and be made of well-made iron, and be toothed to hold them in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains behind, you must put moistened cotton on the place with butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the place is swollen, you must put in forceps called "algefri", with which the head seems to be a duck's bill; and inside they should be made like a file and that is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is fitting that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", i.e., rasp, by which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with it, that's good; if not, you help yourself with all the instruments, by which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has two wings, by which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other pliers which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems a pair of great pincers, whose form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool is to be used except that it cannot break; and know that many are tools of dens; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the wise skilled masters find their instrument themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach a tool because of the diversity of its bones and it is not broken if one searches for the tools that it needs, as I have told you, and with the help of gestures, which is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not slip away, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of medicines appropriate for them, and if there is in the bone rotting, and it is small, one can repair with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the natural body, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary for you to know if the teeth are newly formed after the tooth, and are not in their proper place, and cannot be filed or sharpened: then draw it; and if it is crooked with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and is of iron sharp on one side.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the back of it is blunt and blunt in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, so that you do not move the others, and if it shows itself so that one can file it, then take the file of a similar shape to this form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth bluntly and lightly in your hands, so that it does not move until it scrapes; then smooth out the end completely without any roughness. And if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is knocked out, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot close their mouth over what they are chewing without it falling, and you have cured them with restrictive medicines, but these do not help; then you must constrict it with a thread of gold, for the thread of silver becomes green and rotten, but gold never decays; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size between the teeth; and if you see that the tooth is bent, take the thread and double it between the two sound teeth, then place the roots between the new teeth, if there are one or more, until you have brought them safely to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover it just up to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and safely, until it does not move at all; and tie a ligature to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the wires of the thread to a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and place between the sound tooth and the gum, so that it does not injure the tongue; and then let it stay tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, so bind with another thread. If it remains and serves thus for all its time, and this is the shape of teeth and the figure of the direction of the two sound teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s'en entremette mie qui n'est saiges et soffrans, car les gens d'armes ont trop souvent leur main aux dens des autres pour leur faire des dentelles.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes it happens that this tumor comes under the tongue or by nature, when one is born thus; or from a wound that has healed by accident; and the operations are such as to work on the mouth of the patient, with his head in your sound tooth, and lift up the tongue; then tie off the nervous ligament of the large part, so that the tongue is freed from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, it is from a wound that has healed, so you put the stitch and tie off the large part of this bond; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done it, lift up the head of rosewater and vinegar, or cold water; then place under the tongue a linen tent; and give the patient each night, so that the swelling may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding from the puncture, place verdigris on the wound site; and if the blood continues to flow, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is colored red or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards putridity, and there is moisture, then drain the pus and make an incision with a fine spatula, and deliver it from both sides; and if the bleeding does not stop at your procedure, so apply vitriol broth until it be stopped, then return to your procedure until you have drained all the fluid; then lift up the poultice of aloe and silk, and cure him with other treatments until he be healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que vous me demandiez d'interpréter un texte médical ancien, probablement écrit en français du Moyen Âge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a lump comes up in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called the "amandres"; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and foamy colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also on account of the bleeding; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will part it, or else it would break on its own; and if it is of white colour greenish, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cut it, but first examine whether the abscess has cooled down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his eyes be in the shade, and cover the mouth and take hold of the servant between his hands, and press the tongue beneath all the instrument, by which this is the shape; and it should be of silver or subtle bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue onto the whole instrument, and you see the abscess? Take a thread and insert it into the almond, and leave it so that the thread is above as much as you can; and take nothing from the threads with you, then scrape it with the instrument, of which this is the shape, which resembles a claw; and although the points are curved, and one end the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or silver:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, scrape it with pincers, of which this is the shape... (but I think there's a small mistake in the translation, "de coi ci est li forme" should probably be something like "with jaws that are shaped like...")
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting with a knife on one side and naming on the other side; and when you have cut out one of the swellings, if there is another like it, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water and cold and sweet, and as the bleeding subsides, gargle the patient with water or cooked apple peels or myrtle leaves and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other swellings arise in the throat than the two almonds, if you cut them out like the two almonds carefully.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicined a woman from an abscess that was born inside the throat, that is to say the small abscess; and I had well closed all the throat so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would be dead if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had burst through two openings of the birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and I inserted a needle into one opening, then the liquid flowed out, and in it there was a large portion of pus; then I reinserted the other part into the other birth opening, and I tied the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that I inserted the needle into the abscess, and extracted some of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus was the passage of the throat opened for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, and filled the place that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I bound it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus she remained without growth; and I left her parties, and knew only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	C'est une référence à un passage du texte original !
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the swelling descends to the eye, and it is inflamed and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under the eyebrow and rounded, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the inflamed abscess has been eased, and it is subtle, then you should cauterize it; and the one which is round and assembled but is not long; and it is bloody or of dark color or black, then you should cut out the incision from it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger over the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is then necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, concerning its redness and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we made a reminder here before; then insert the reed into the eye, and draw it out, and cut out at the points of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover too much of the superfluous substance that exceeds the natural term; for if you do so, you will grieve at the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is sound.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about covering, then you must use an expedient in the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts their head in your vein, and then presses the tongue to the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cautery, and fasten with a piece of live coal, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and take hold of the handle of this instrument, by which it is shaped:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say the chief a hair or a piece of cloth put the medicine on it, like the bristles of a comb, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand all over the medicine and press on the eye with the quantity of half an hour, until you see it blackened and the medicine's irritation is calmed; and if you see any inflammation, take cotton and wrap it around an instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument all over the cotton in the cavity above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry and sleep afterwards for four or five days. And if you need to start the cauterization of the medicine again, then start it again, and after that cauterize the area around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean up what is around the medicine; and be risen from cold water, and be cured of gargarismes until you are healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	Cette phrase semble être un extrait d'une recette médicale ancienne. Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. de squinance	De squinance (note: I'm assuming this is a single sentence)
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who are swooning, it is necessary that the cut of the throat, which is called "epiglottis", be uncovered; and one should not aid by this means, because all the veins and the pulse of the sick person are near to those who have swallowed something hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two hands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the ruin that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision through and through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision from the surface, not in the cartilage; and those places are conversable to the section of the epiglottis which have no flesh, and the vessels are long enough for it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, so it must be that he extends the skin of the throat to all the surrounding area, then cuts through the skin as far as the chin; and pours out the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the slit, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein from the chin which bursts forth through the place that is broken, and by the defect of the voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since we doubted strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound of the skin and sew it all whole except for the cartilage; then administer medications that make flesh grow back, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I think it's said that we should not do this just as much until the throat is completely stopped and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default is in vain.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus it is guarded from death; and for this reason command the ancients to leave the wound open as long as the malice of the disease has not passed, and it passes in three days or four. Then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took a dagger, and pierced it in her throat, and cut out part of the channels from the privy member; and I was called to cure her, and I found her thus dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that she had not cut too narrow or shallow a wound in her throat, and the veins were torn apart by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healed; and there came upon the maiden fever only that she turned red in the voice, and returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of a large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is in two ways, of which one is similar to a fat nodule, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it does not seem right to operate with fire unless in him who is small, and examine and search thoroughly: if you find it just as I have said, fat, and cannot be cut in any way, then cut it, just as one cuts a nodule, and treat all around its cloth, if there is none; and search well throughout, and cure it just as it should, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the lymph nodes
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways for us that I will say all the similarities; and now it behooves me to say the whole difference which is between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, until the boil has passed, and the corruption has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the boil there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins as well as a grape, and becomes large; and they are of two kinds, either fatty, or moist, and very much colored are such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the node, that you probe and examine it first with all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", according to what shape or form it may take, which is later followed by the "chapitre".
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of incising abscesses from boils is that you take or the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your double-ended instrument back and forth until you know that the instrument has pierced to the core, then as it should be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and take care lest something escapes.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moist discharge comes from a tumor, whatever its color may be, then treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards the intercommunicator does not come out with moisture, know that it is fatty, so then treat it in cross shape, and take hold of it with forceps, and peel off lightly from each part, and to the linen where it lies let you draw it sound with new thread; and if you cannot draw it sound, then draw it apart in pieces such that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there remains nothing, it will return the pus many times; and if there remains a small amount and the blood grieves it, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders hot, and bind the wound, and put on soothing things to warm the abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is sound; and if the pus is great, then cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure it from those that inflame the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is too painful or in some other way contrary to you, then hasten and apply the area with vinegar broth, and leave it for two or three days until the wound has purged, and let the ebullition of blood subside; then return to cutting out what remains of the node.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the forms of the inserted instruments, and they are of three kinds: great and medium and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulae; and they are also like the needles with which one stitches scrofula, and they are made of citrine iron, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most proven for stitching black boils to enclose the swellings of fistulae; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the width of the pores.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the lancets are of many likenesses, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are lancets with two handles of three kinds also; and there are lancets with three handles, and they are also of three kinds; and there are lancets with one handle alone, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these cuts are incisions, and there are such that do not cut very far in one part, from which we skin the nerves, so that we do not strike the vein or the nerve; and they are introdusables [?], made in mittens, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one should not use them too far from a healthy area, such as legs, arms, and breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes we make another instrument that is small, resembling skin scrapers, in this shape, by which we stop bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed in any place that heals after cutting of veins and arteries, and they are made according to this great shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem to be women's breasts; and they remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wants to cure them, must know how to do it according to this shape from line b to line g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with medicine in pouring charcoal, then sew together the two lips of the wound at costure, and care for it until it is healed; and if the nipple inclines downward, and is swollen because of its size as happens to women, so make it into two folds above, by two similar tears; from which one will be joined to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, down to the line .b. just to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and do what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding of blood, so you must fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it has softened the remaining fat and skin, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The swellings of the haunches.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard forms of scrofula or they have ribs, and those that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who are moisty shall be cupped according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the juice that is in the abscess has been drained, put ointment on the wound with clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then take out all the cotton and treat it with salve as needed until they are healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like forms of scrofula, treat them as we have said in cuts of scrofula, and if they are running with juice, apply a cauterizing agent as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is obstructed and the skin above it is sewn up, there are often abscesses; and just as well, he has a vein swollen and an abscess; and if you recognize it in this way when it's because of the artery, then the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel it strongly; and when it's because of the vein, it appears to be far off; and it would be foolishness to cauterize this abscess, just as much when it is under the armpits and the angles and the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must avoid the fire cure, and also that which is at the head, and in him who has a swelling of the artery fill up over the skin with long cloth; then work the incision on the veins, and carefully separate the artery from the threads, so that it is uncovered; then insert below one needle, and make it pierce to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then prick the place between the two threads with an introducer until the pus comes out that is there, and so be freed the abscess; then apply the cure that makes the blood coagulate, so that the thread comes undone; then treat those with ointments suitable for them, until they are healed; and if the abscess is because of the vein's incision, it is necessary that you mark on your hand what you can take from the abscess all over the skin, then insert a needle below the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there will be one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I told you, with one of the two parts tied to the two threads of the file; and if you doubt that the filaments do not come out, then reinsert another needle through all the filament below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the filaments in four places; then cauterize the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cauterize the excess flesh and leave what is tied; then put on a damp cloth soaked in vinegar and oil, then apply treatments with tents and ointments until they are healed.
des apostemes des ners	The boils of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like boils come on the arm and in the vein, boils also come on the neck when they are heated, or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more often in the joints and in the hands and in all places where there are articulations, and it is a grievous swelling, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one tightens it strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and that which is in articulations does not need to be cut with iron: perhaps there would be a contraction; and he who is in the head or in the forehead, make the skin burst at the sutures.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is small, take hold of it with forceps and cut off its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a thread, and scorch it, then burn out the bone and assemble the wound to the incision, and care for it until it be healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere at all, this is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and there are thin roots and large heads; and I have seen one man who had two fungi in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had small roots, and were already split open, and were always moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 pounds, and in the incision, it is that you observe whether the patient's body is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist with a thin root; if it cuts to the spatula wide, and there are in your presence the cautery over fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the blood ceases, then you hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient shivering and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made linen thread, and bind the tumor as we have said, and let it be for two days; and then restrain it, and cease not to strain the linen thread until it cuts through the tumor, and cut by its own weight; and if the roots are large, then fear to cut into them at all for the belly, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not recur; then cure the wound, and take care that you do not cut the tumor which is of foul color and poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of a boil in the next chapter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is full-grown
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	The appearance of the boil comes from a cautery of a wound or tearing of the lymph node, and is above the belly and in some of the boils, as it happens in other wounds, or bleeding from veins or arteries according to what is before, or by windiness; and if this is due to the rupture of the lymph node and by the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and clear with diverse exit.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is very diverse. When you press it with your fingers it swells back up, and then returns, and by chance it may be inflamed, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for great pain.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and clear well when you press it with your hand, and do not hold back; and if it is due to bleeding, then it will appear by these signs the abscess is large and hard, and sticks out in accordance with an amount; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to touch, and the operations are such that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of the artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I said in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or bowel, you must instruct the patient to stretch his gut and be straightened all the way out; then sign around the belly; then command him to lie flat between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with all the surrounding tissue; then cut the half of the abscess above up to the large ligature; then tie it around with a strong thread or a tight silk cord securely, and let the rest of the wound be loosened; then work on the half of the abscess extended over the ligature, and put your right index finger inside, and try to find the intestine; if you find it caught by the ligature, release it, and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowel, take hold of the ligature, and cut off the excess part; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the two needles through what you have done in a cross shape so that it is perforated; then pull the abscess into four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it has healed, and scoop out the dead flesh by itself; or cut it when it becomes small and has opened up, then cure what needs to be cured, and remove the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	A new chapter! It seems we've finished discussing abscesses (apostemes) and are moving on to treating boils or chancre. Would you like me to summarize what we've discussed so far?
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We've discussed the characteristics of a boil (chancre) in our previous sections, and how to treat it with medicines. We also mentioned that one should be careful when treating boils that are located in sensitive areas or near vital organs.
