Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with hot water or broth and cook it well, because through this the entrance becomes free of anything; and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch in the wound using the instrument with which we lance boils; and the first treatment is to make an incision, which none of us should do without great necessity, for it is the instrument to cut: if you cut inside at the curve and outwards not, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then put them back in place according to their natural shape in their proper location, if you are able, for that helps a lot.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part under the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part under the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly put what I say about the belly wound in one of these two parts so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to heed what I say for big and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Put on what is available to you, then take between your hands the thread that fills the entire wound with its hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common method of suturing, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave a space at the head of the wound equal in length to two fingers, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two eyes of the skin with the two eyes of the siphac, which is underneath the skin on the inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two heads of the siphac the four together; then pull out a double thread around the needle of two parts, then assemble the two lips of the wound properly, and then leave a space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you tied the first needle, and do not cease doing this with the needles, until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be middle-sized, between fine and coarse, because fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot well enter: for this reason they should be middle-sized; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound in front of the suturing; then tie off the eyes of the needles, so they do not prick the patient at night, and I put tents or cloths on the eyes of the needles for their ease, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this method of suture with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because one needle suffices, or two: the second suturing is common, and it is that you assemble the two eyes of the skin and the two eyes of the siphac together on a needle where there is strong middle thread; and when you have pierced these holes all four together, then take out the needle at the part where you began, in the manner in which one sews clothes; and put a space between each stitch equal to the size of a large thumb, this suturing is known among people, and I sewed up a wound that belonged to an ox had on its belly, which was injured with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's length great, and there were intestines well two palms long inside it, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back to his intestines after it had been 24 hours full, and the wound was sewn up just to 15 days, and I healed him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in this place where you could not find any, nor any medicine; and I put clean cotton above the wound two times a day, and I washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle, and push it from the outer part just to the inner part; when it has pierced straight through right in right, then pull out the head of the thread or suture where you had pushed the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part just to the outer part; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew as quailers make their pelts, and you leave a turn on one side and take it up on the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks call properly, is such that some people do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this way: take a needle or point of a thimble nearby, and make it pierce only that place, and let the two ends of the thread remain; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part just up to the inner part, at both ends of the thread; then make it pierce one end and the other end, from the outer part just up to the inner part, in two other holes of the thimble that are on the opposite side; and this is the more correct manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this phrase, and some testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the rupture is on the belly, then the suture is more grievous than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such that as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as fire has changed it, then put in front the intestine, and the cloth; then put on powdering charcoal dust, and if fire has changed it, then put on any present ointment until the wound heals; tie the thread, and sew together the edges of the skin, and the flesh; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put in front, at once when it begins to heal, old cotton, and stir it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not form community with the principal members, it is necessary that you bathe linen cloth lightly in tempered hot oil, or in rosed oil, and place it around the armpits, and under the shoulders; and if it feels pain or irritation in the bowels, and many times happens, then cleanse them with black wine tincture, and indeed if the irritation comes just to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily healed than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and it is because of the delicacy of the veins that are in them, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the arrow jumps out of the wound, replace it in the same way as the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you must tie the part that is black so that blood does not come there, because there are veins and arteries; then take what is between the tie and hang the two ends down from the lower part of the wound as far as possible to ease the extraction when the arrow jumps out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen a man who was wounded with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and was sewn up and became a fistula, and there came forth feces and gas; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and the hole closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him being stitched, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his stomach; and there was no evil, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take a thread from great flaxen threads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, place it over the two lips, so that it straitens its mouth there; and then beat the head with it, and it will stay as if it cannot be untied, then put another thread after in this manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Those intestines are attached in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is sewn from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is well peeled, and then bind it to the head of this thread a thin linen thread twisted around it, then insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and straighten it in its proper place; and this manner of sewing with intestines has no other way than according to faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is on one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or healing except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be;
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows in age, is called universally "fistula", and similarly when it is hollowed out and forms a pouch.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true and hard white nodule formation where one does not feel pain, and it is also hollowed out like a bird's feather; and sometimes it forms a clear pouch, and other times it is thick; sometimes small, and other times quite large; and I have spoken about all these things in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only because of one of the nine causes: that is to say, by the weakness of blood or body; or by its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the skin, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pouching; or the place is putrid, and the matter has bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region delays digestion, and delays healing, and flees by nature; or it has veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I tell you about the remedy for fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas that occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the major veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the spleen, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus that which comes to the principal property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous cure, and there is no other remedy but digging and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come exactly to the place that I said, and you have faith in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of lead or iron; if the fistula is straight, cut it; and if the fistula is twisted, search for it with a subtle probe of steel, because steel bends around twisting; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well probe it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the holes, because moisture runs from one hole to another, and purify it; then cut out as much as you know, whether there is bone or nerve, and is it deep in the body, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or a vein, or in any of the places that I told you, then cut it out according to what I told you, and remove the false humor and the corrupted flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep enough from the right place, then it is necessary that you cut it out deeper than that, as much as you can, then put wet tents in medicine juice, and fill them up to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put unguents in fresh flesh, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize it just as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or artery does not bleed or if the principal limbs are unharmed, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it clean until all the corruption is removed, then treat with things that draw out humors until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and turn back to what was before, know that you have not proceeded far enough: uncover and scrape as deep as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course; and if there is only a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with pincers, then remove it with the instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then draw them all out, do not leave any of them; and if moisture makes opposition, and there is no error or fear, then cut and scrape and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something causing irritation, and let it be so that the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily removed; and if it's a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, just stop the corruption until all blackness is gone from the bone, then treat the wound; and if there is great part of corruption, and it comes right to the marrow of the bone; so you must scrape and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it be sewed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that you take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was the young man around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, so that the materials came to the leg and he was afflicted with a large abscess, and there was no way to open it outside; but the surgeons through their foolishness worked on it for so long that the abscess opened up and a lot of material flowed out, and became a fistula, and there came out many holes from which all kinds of pus and moisture from the body were flowing; and many surgeons put treatment around 2 years, and there was not any wise person in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed out through the holes with a great amount of pus; and his body became red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent over one of the ulcers, and then examined all the ulcers, and found that one was coming into contact with another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and dug into one of the ulcers until I uncovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption was coming right up to the bone inside; I removed what appeared from the corrupted bone, and I thought there would be no other corruption except for that which I had removed; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, and it could not heal; and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I thought about joining the bone together; but I couldn't until I dug around a palm's length of the bone, and pulled the bone back to its full shape, then I treated it with medicines; and he was healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to start again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood it often poured out, but it was entirely healed, and in place of the bone there grew a hard skin, and it was in good condition and had no harm or contraindication at all, neither to eat nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be set up like this: take a linen cloth and stretch it over the end of the bone that is open, and command someone to hold it up; and put another thicker linen cloth on top of the skin above the bone, and tie it so that you draw out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the healthy skin at the place where you want to see; lest the saw cut into the healthy skin. And take a reed or a flat instrument and put it under the bone to cover up the corrupt flesh; and you must set until you can see and feel the corruption, and set again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover the flesh entirely; then place a burning stick underneath, and then use a needle to draw out the corruption from one part to another, and the needle should be as long as the length of the corruption is deep, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut into the corrupted joint, and clean out the bone where it contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, then there is no other agent but to cut into it; and if the corruption is in the wrist or in the ankle of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about the corrosion, how it opens; and cleanse it in every way that you can, but that the vein or the nerve does not hinder you; and know that the cutting instrument and the needles for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of operation; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; so ponder on the instrument which you have need of, according to what is required.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints can be spoiled either from within or from outside; and when you have medicated that corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not bring profit, then you must cover that member down to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the greater evil, the failure of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, as if they were burned with fire, and after the blackness, it swells again in that member, and takes hold all over the body; then hasten to cover, and if this corruption is in the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give any hope of coming to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, then cut off at the joint, so that the corruption does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cut it off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there's no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and do thusly with it when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut the whole foot; and if it rises into the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there's no other device except for hastening to kill the patient with a surer death; and the manner of cutting off or cauterizing the member is that you bind it above and below, and extend one servant of the ligature downward, and another servant of the ligature upward, and you loosen the flesh that is between the two ligatures by one spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize, and put a linen cloth from each side so that the cauterization does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient with another lesion and abscess there.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if hemorrhaging comes from the cut when you work, then cauterize the place immediately, or put some restraining powder on it; then come back to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my region: he got a gangrene that seemed like a spark of fire, and that corruption came first to his toe of the foot, so much that it took over the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed; and a long time after that the corruption returned in the hand, and he came to me, and I put things reflective after the cleansing of the body on him, and the corrosion could not stop; and he wished that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of reflecting the matter; and I also doubted if I were to amputate his hand, that he would die, for the virtues of man are weak; and he became desperate altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have not concealed this tale except that it should be told so that others may learn from it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Occasionally an abscess forms in the fatty part of the skin, and remains so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; and then they swell and burst, and the pus shoots out, leaving the place empty, as is the case with a wineskin; and the skin on top is just as thin as delicate fabric, and does not go all the way to the bone, or all the way to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone deep within, then it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut around that skin entirely, and especially when it is thin, just like delicate fabric; and it should not be treated because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin is suppurating, and the corruption is not deep within, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cut around it with a caustic like this: see if the breast is large, and the boil which comes out has a foul odor, then make an Egyptian medicine like this: take aloes, oil, and lapis lazuli equally, and put the mixture in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and apply the medicine to the breast, and press on the boil; and leave the medicine there for two hours, then strain it out; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and sometimes a caustic of ash water is made, when this medicine is not present, and it's that you take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water over them, then let it cool, and use it as a caustic, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash water, then make a caustic with water and honey or there's a bit of lapis lazuli to be added; or you make a caustic with honey and sweet wine so that the honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the boil suppurate; and when you have done this, and you have confidence that the breast is well cleansed, then make a caustic of those things which cause flesh to grow in it, and it's that you take defnite plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you make a caustic with some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have spoken about the treatment of ointments; and if the boil of the breast is small, and the tube of the caustic cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a iron piece, and put on a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then close it and leave just enough room for the caustic to enter, and if the boil that comes out is above, then cut or lower the place where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is fully in place, let no flesh grow there; and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see it, arrange so that the bow runs to the lowest point where it is, because when the bow is fully in place, let no flesh grow there and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see it, then arrange thus: that the bow runs lightly downwards and lets nothing of the bow remain; and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast, and sit above the linen cloth that covers all the breast; then cut at the most forceful point the pustule on the breast which is larger than the first, pour ointment softly above the other cloth according to the size of the pustule, and place it above the pustule of the breast to ease the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside that after many days once; and that which is above the pustule on the breast, take away often to loosen the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or much or little, or digested or undigested; and be aware if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that bursts on the pustule of the breast, then know that the breast has healed already, and approach the health; and then release it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you free the wound, then change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast continues to discharge undigested pus for a good while, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons have coursed after a long time, you should not despair of health, for the health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who recover from flesh in their wounds after a long time, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested chyme bursts forth from the chest after many days, know that the lungs have not healed; and if the lungs delay to heal and become inflamed, take dry medicines with moist substance and dry virtue, such as defrutum diaphanum, for it contains a great part of vinegar, and that is the last medicine; take defrutum diaphanum and mix it with rose oil and equal parts of old wine; then cook it and use it; and similarly make thickened honey, when defrutum diaphanum is not present, or you take myrrh, aloes, and incense, and crush them, and powder them on the honey while it is over the fire; and then apply it to a cloth and attach it to the chest; and at some time administer Aristolochia longa, and roots of heavenly lily, which is also like the flour of vetches and centaury; and use simples or compounds: crush them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption has penetrated deep, and made an impression in the bone, or in hard limbs, or in ligaments; so treat it with fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the lung.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A pilus cyst comes from under the nail of the finger or foot, or perhaps it occurs in other places; and when it is grown old and no care is taken to it, if the abscess bursts, the boil runs and discharges pus as long as the root of the nail goes, and perhaps all the way through; and comes the corrosion right up to the bone, so that there is a foul odor, and the joint of the thumb is wide, and the color is putrid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away from there all the dead part that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, begins to prick and cut it, then you must put a hot iron under the nail that pricks the flesh, and hold it up high, and carefully and lightly cut out that flesh, and apply medicines that burn and corrode in order to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the ulcer is in the bone, then cut it, and take away, because as long as the bone is corrupted within it, so cannot heal; and if you see the tooth corrupting, then cut into it at the same spot as before said, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is festered, and inflamed, and it feels great pain, then you must first cleanse it; then cut the angle of the spatula awry over, and be careful that the blade does not go up to the flesh which is under the ulcer, because the patient would feel too great a pain; and if it happens, put something on top that calms.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The teeth that arise in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a tooth or he has bones, and sometimes there is a tooth, and any of them arise in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the teeth.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any defect in the two kneecaps cannot move them, and he who is born with a deformation of the joint of the kneecap, by chance can move them; the shape of him who is fat is light, in such a manner: let it be cut in its root of a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is heavy to cure, and you must be careful when cutting him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or grows a boil on the backside, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh to the bone first, then cut the bone with a thread suitable for this, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the tongue in combination come from birth, or from a blow to the wound, or from burns of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam, so that the part that was torn repairs itself according to its natural form; then put between two tents or damp cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is sewn up, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes to any part of his tongue with the palm, then cut out that swelling in such a way.
des vils	from evil things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	A swelling is a large enveloped mass filled with melancholy superfluities that come on many members of the body; and it more often occurs in the legs of those who walk and work and carry heavy loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary to administer him a purging of gall, and then cleanse him with the sap of the basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is done in two manners: one is that you clip them off and bleed out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the swelling and cut it all through.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first arise the leg with a sharp iron point very hot, until the large vein is subtlety cut; then restrain the patient's leg from above the knee as far as the part below the kneecap; then clip the swelling in one place or two or three places with a wide incision; then raise and bleed out the black blood into your hand from one end to the other, until such time as there is as much blood issuing as the virtue of the patient can endure; and then bind it, and command him that he eat eating cold black meat; and repeat the evacuation and purging when the swellings are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s'il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d'aigue chaude tant qu'elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and coiled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not cover it over; and treat it in the manner which we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one covers the vein is curved, and does not cut into it, so that one may cover the vein; and it is a thick curve, for if it were slender, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the thighs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry earth; and it may also arise elsewhere than in the thighs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as snakes and worms come within the body between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this abscess are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the area changes, and the abscess begins to come out, just like a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the abscess bursts open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth about one to two inches thick and the thickness of three fingers, and leave the cloth at the leg, and every time it drips blood in the back, you will wrap around the cloth, and the bandage; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap up the rest, and do not cut it at its root, until it comes out completely; for if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and makes an abscess and rotting or boils in the area, and bad disease; for this reason it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until it comes out, and no part remains in the body; and sometimes this abscess when it is treated two palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once, whose it came out ten palms long, and when you cut it, there are several holes or sores, and it pierces through to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the material inside is emptied out, and medicine is applied to the area every day, until it heals like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time there is a swollen vein, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or on the foot, and much pus comes out, and from which rain comes out; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "disease of an ox", because it has often affected bulls, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body going up and down, and feels very bad when it moves from member to member, until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and comes out; and it is infected with the corruption of some humors, such as worms and serpents and lice and tapeworms in the stomach; and one doubts its wickedness, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance gets inside, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, one cannot force it to be still when it wants to: so then you must tie the place above and below with a strong string tightly, then strike up on top of it and draw it out thoroughly; and if the abscess is deep in the flesh and you don't find it, then cauterize it with fire above, until it boils; and the greatest harm that it does is that it will run into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head of the eye, you must hold a thread tightly underneath it, then strike up on top, and draw it out thoroughly; and it is necessary to use the patient with cleansing of the body with dissolving medicines for foul humors, and abstain from rank food that brings putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain which comes from windiness (or a wind)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in certain members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and I soon after saw it rise, just as a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like sharp silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after ran all through the body, so much that she came to the other arm; then she told me that she had been turning around her body again and again, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this illness act in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had often seen that the pain was well transferred from one place to another, but I did not see it so in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman's body was dry, and her veins were hidden, and for that reason that constriction appeared; and they do not notice according to this reason in those who are lubricous, and who have moist bodies and responded veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it makes them open up as we have said, then bind on top and below hastily; and then cut on top until the swelling constrains itself back into place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with those who suppress the swellings, such as fetid pills, and snake root pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points and small ones, hooked, and barbed; and those with two angles, and those with handles, and those with pieces; and the one that lodges in any member does so in two manners: either in a principal member it lodges, such as brain, heart, liver, womb, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later is apparent: so you must beware of extracting this arrow, because death follows in many dispositions; and when this bad sign is not apparent to you, and the arrow is not deeply imbedded, then pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and penetrates the bone, and bursts the scull vein which is above the brain, is when there is scotoma and redness and swelling and convulsion in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it issues from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps the speech and voice are lost; and a white and moist wound erupts like a boil, and also as if burned by fire; and when you see this sign, beware of cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow wound when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it were stuck in something hard rather than soft; and perchance the arrow moves back and forth like a hair, and there is dark blood oozing out, and chills and cold sweat, and faintness: then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that hits the stomach is that foam comes out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps high and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow hits the covering of the back, it is near the small ribs; and it emits great anguish and great pain and gasping, and the movement affects all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the abdomen and pus comes out through the intestine's route, then there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows away, and the sick person feels a very strong pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and wrists and legs and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not venomous, as I'll tell you happened to me, so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him on the eyelid at its root near the nose: I tried it and extracted it from the other side below the fatty part of the ear, and he recovered without sequel.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I extracted an arrow from a child that struck him in the fatty part of the eye below the paper-thin skin, and the arrow was bent, and could only be drawn out by the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all made of iron without ears; the child recovered, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I drew out the feathers, and made it subtle until I pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the home, that had pierced the belly, and I thought he was going to die; and then after 30 days, his condition didn't change; I cut around the arrow, and bound it, and pulled it out, and there wasn't a bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen on the back, and the wound was sewn up above; and the arrow remained inside him, and didn't change his natural condition, nor did it find harm in any of his natural workings.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.
