And you see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and thus he remained without suffering great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow that is lodged in the home of the prince's king, which was shot into his neck, and was somewhat leaning to the right side; and the arrow was entirely retracted I was called to treatment after it had been lodged for 3 days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with a fine touch and did not feel it; and he felt puncturing and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on him a plaster that attracts and digests, so that the place does not become inflamed; and the wound of the arrow became visible.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put a plaster on him for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient stayed in this way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I apply a medicinal astringent by hand every day, until the wound is open; and I examined it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which was protruding at its base; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicine astringent, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and it passed well through the terminus within 4 months, and then burst out so much blood that I had to insert forceps on both sides and could not come out; at which point I did not cease to refine and invent various devices, until I grasped it one day with forceps well-made, according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you put your cure on what I do not say; for a book cannot contain all things; but wise masters discover much in small things, and those present and lacking, find new work, and new instrument, at the removal of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not emerge from limbs or are stuck in them except in two ways: either by the place where they enter or on the other side; and that which jumps out through the place where it entered is an arrow entering fleshy parts, and often jumps out.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, then let it stay until the flesh is rotten around it and the wound is opened; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then let it stay like that for some days and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it doesn't come out, then cut through all the surrounding flesh with a very sharp instrument, until the place around it is enlarged, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said occur to the patient: do not pull it out at all, but leave it until it has been even for several days, because if the arrow comes close to the sphenoid, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come as far as the sphenoid, and the patient stays for some days without bad accident, then you may pull out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out, then administer theriac around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and cannot be seen, search for it throughout the tent; and if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, cut away until the wound is large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in there from two parts up to where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't get it out in one go, then leave it until the area around is rotten, and then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding is contrary to you, follow what we have said about treatment in this chapter; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and learn how you can pull out the arrow without danger soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape he was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid it is possible to give, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or it breaks through any part of him, or the skin is swollen in the area where you can see or feel it obviously: cut then above, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out; if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around so that it goes into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is in it, push it all the way to the shaft; and if the shaft slips and you see that you should administer a draft, administer the instrument with a spike, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is stuck, push the instrument in with a pointed end into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, then you should cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it requires.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in or near the hip, or belly, or bladder, or side, and you can see it, then cut above it; and be careful not to cut the vein or the nerve, and then pull it out, and then close the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers with which we pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, small, and tiny, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the feathers of a bird, to throw at the point of the arrow, such as this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for binding and piercing is such as this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins in the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins through which one is healed there are XXXI, of which XVI are on the head, namely: two vessels that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the upper corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is on the back of the neck; and the two jugular veins that are in the throat; and two veins that are above the lips near the mouth, and they are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins whose cutting is commonly used are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is located on the left side, and people call it the "vein of the head"; and the second is called the "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and people call it the "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is located on the right side, and people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and it is this one that is cut, which opens up manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the thumb and the little finger, and it has two branches; and on the leg and the foot are three veins: one that is under the fold of the skin on the left side, and the second is the superficial which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "saphenous", which is at the ankle on the other side; and on the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloody vessel behind the ears that helps the ancient cathartics and migraine sufferers; and the quality of the bloodletting is such that you raise the patient's head, and wipe the area where the vessels are with a rough cloth; then tie the patient's neck to a string so that the two vessels appear behind the ears in two dependent places under the head: which will be your guide, and where you feel the pulse below your elbow, bind it down tightly; then take the lancet and insert it into the vessel as far as the bone, then raise your hand all the way up to the vessel and strike both the skin and the vessel in two places at a right angle, and make the blood come out until you see it; then tie and bind it so that it is healed; and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting from the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth an old, and sour, and habitual eye infection, and for the eyes; and the quality of the bloodletter is such as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feels the hair under your chin, and then signs to him to begin; then lift the needle above the vein in the direction of your index finger, and push the lancet down, and lift up the vein high, and cut, as you have done in the other two veins, and do according to the blood flow that suits your need; then release the patient, and put your chin on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have also spoken of their closing and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the blood of the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face and in headache and in gout; and its quality is that the patient twists his neck so tightly that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and pinch with your hand, or another thing, and let two blood vessels flow according to the amount you see; then tie off the patient's neck vein, and bind the vein so that it is stopped and no more work on a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the bandages are too tight; and the vein heals crookedly, because the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the bandages when they are stretched thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the armpits helps with the eyes, and the itch, and the scabies, and the gout in the eye, and the maladies of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting some string, as before; then he bleeds, and the bleeding should be through the middle of the vein a bit long and a bit wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandages are thin, perhaps they will break; then make up with blood as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the neck vein is worth against ague and sudden dropsy, and maladies of the face, such as headache and itch that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes a thin flame, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of two gum resins is helpful in tightening the veins, and at the beginning of treatment, and in many diseases, and swelling, and corrosion, and herpes, and boils; and the quality of the salve is that the patient ties his neck with a cloth under one and the other, as we have said; and the master stands on the head of the sick person, and the sick person sits on the seat, then he opens the vein of the long one somewhat widely, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then makes another incision in the other vein, then unties the ligature, and holds the veins steadily so that the patient does not strangle; and leaves him until morning, that the wound be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins of the upper lips is helpful for boils in the mouth, and for corruption of gums, and splits in the lips, and on the neck and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the salve is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, where one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by being black, and by having small black veins around them: then cut both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, so cut the thicker one of each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cleansing under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood from the veins that are under the tongue is a great help after the cleansing of the head, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the surgeon is such that the patient must sit in his hands before the sun, and lift up the tongue, and look under each side at a black vein: cleanse then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for there are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck, from which one commonly cleanses, are cleansed in two manners: either with a burning iron that is quite wide and fiery, or an olive-green subtlety like surgeons' knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the thick bandage is well-known, and it's wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick and clear blood, and contain thick and murky blood; and this is the form of the olive-like flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more delicate and pointed, and is for healing the thin veins where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, is useful for diseases that are located under the throat, and around the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary to bleed with a lancet, and beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I said; and one should not grasp the flame, but cut with forceps.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then it is necessary to extract it, and change another one; or you want some of its length, or bleed in place of it from the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with forceps at the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, it is thus necessary that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the place as far as you can feel the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and bind up the arm, and cut the vein above the flameless (or below) the silver probe; and beware that you do not strike in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: draw back then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulging upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and place your thumb above for a long time, then remove your thumb if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind up the arm, and let it be so, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move it until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes to you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, for the head will retreat; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a peel of fig tree, and make it soft, and take one half and bind well on to the other joint; if the blood is stopped, it's good; if not, then heal it with the powder that stops bleeding, as we have said; and the stopping of blood is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the neck is so strong that it can stop blood from the top of the head and from the lower body, because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to beware for the nerve which is below, and if he probes too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells up and the vein gets inflamed, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve opens very often, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, then you must loosen the veins with the instrument anesil; and pull out the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has veins between the two nerves, then burn them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bloodletting from the cephalic vein is helpful, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and you must bleed with a burning olive branch or a burning myrtle twig, for this is the most safe of all veins, since there are no nerves nor arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, you must seek the most suitable position and do not harm anything if it is not found the first time, and then continue; and by chance, some men's veins swell when it is done for the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the healing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not done except for the purpose of preserving health and preventing coming illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are open: that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bloodlet in the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bloodlet on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who administers medicine has no fixed hour determined, but when there is need of the day or night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not necessary to treat children up to XIV years, nor women carrying fruit that they have been pregnant for more than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should those who have passed 60 years be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be treated, however it may be, it is necessary that they empty their intestines with a light clyster, if they have much bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw out from the intestines the superfluities which are harmful to the main members; and he does not get cured who is too full of meat, nor who is drunk until further, nor dropsy-ed; and if someone has been sick after a passion of colic, and vomiting, and disturbance of the belly, and often abiding with woman, and labor, waking, and sleeping, and all that virtue, or by something of the arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if the disease is thick, through meat and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood, and treat the woman's womb around the third part, as we have said; and guard that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the physician be higher than he who is being treated, and moisten the arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature above gently, for when it is too tight or too loose, so it cannot correct the disease; and then rub the arm with the hands, until the veins become swollen, and are felt; then wet the physician's hand with the flame of a spoonful of old oil; then put his fist on top of that woman's womb below the place where he wants to treat her, so that the womb does not flee or fall when piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and there are such that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on fire, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of them; and if one opens the vein, it is too narrow a wound, therefore the surgeon should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts on the first time, it's good; and if not, then he starts again a little below or above that place where they were swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed, and the patient is frightened, then leave it alone for a day or two, and do not bind the arm: perhaps there will come abscesses to boil. Do not have him enter a bath, then resume the dressing if he pleases; and if the wound is small, let the blood flow subtly, and you doubt whether it will not be as much blood as you see, so fix in that opening all the flame directly; and do the work hurriedly, indeed while the swelling is inflamed; for this has happened many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling increased, do not start the wound dressing again, and put some linseed oil on it, because it lightens the body of blood, and is wet in this place with the oily cloth; and thus administer linseed oil to each wound that you dress the veins for to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing does triacle and beech resin do when you put them on the swelling; so subtly clean and separate the pus as it becomes too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if it comes to a large abscess that has formed many times, especially when the wound dressing is not yet strong enough for that time or the opening of the vein is small, then be hasty and put a wet sponge on the place in hot water and on a cloth, and bind it for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if it remains on the place after some days with any blackness or greenness, it does no harm; and if you see anything, put something of aloes or myrrh remade in juice of calaminth, monk's pepper, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times has pustule and appearance to the healing of the boil: then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put on any of what we have said, for perhaps it cuts the blood from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it ooze out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it come out until it becomes thinned; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	It is necessary for him who is strong and able, and in need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and the flaps should be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he needs to be healed slowly and often, and one must heal him by cutting across, not piercing; and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging of blood and from severing of nerves, and it is worth more than the healing with a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is weak from bloodletting, it is necessary to give him moist bread in juice of unripe pomegranates; if he is overheated, make a poultice with the blood three times or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, make a poultice in sweet syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he beats against the wound, after the flow of bad blood has stopped, it is necessary that he smokes a meat broth and a subtle perfumed syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of venom.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to ease his arm, and mend it again, so it is necessary, when it is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed a little bit at a time, according to the quantity of his virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to ease his arm after the first bleeding, and it is very firm, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another place, then he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much bad blood inside the body that has already been heated up and made feverish; so it needs to be drawn out in large quantity, and the wound should be enlarged as far as possible until it reaches the pustule; then you must follow all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on top of the pustules when they heal, so that death does not come instead of the pustule, and this happens many times when the healer is neglectful; and it should not happen when you see the arm untied and bloody blood comes out the second time, and the wound is closed, that you press hard on it; nor if it is crooked, that it be stretched hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or put a needle to the tip of the flame, so that the frozen pus that has congealed comes out of the wound and put a poultice made from wet silk on top of it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swelled, then leave him alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed again the second time, then let him bleed in the same spot, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the temporal vein because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The manner of the cure is this: the patient puts his hand in hot water until the scab is red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well; then the wound should be cleaned now through the puncture, not too wide or long; and the holes should be large, and the blood should be cleansed well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, you put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood remain in the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not put the hand in hot water again, because it is more prone to frost than in summer; and this wound's cure is safer from all other wounds that there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure of the swelling of the right hand is worth to all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the wound appears empty; if you see it, then clean the wound from across, and if you cut it completely, nothing will harm; and do not go too deep because the nerves are under all naked of flesh, and then put the hand in hot water again, if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn off as much blood as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and silk to solder it quickly, and do this with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting from the left hand is worth for the disease of melancholy, and do all just as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The swab of the sponge is worth for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its swab is that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein so that it breaks, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and there are many nerves going up from the foot; then swab the one more swollen nerve, or at the ankle, which is most worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bloodlet above the foot, it will warn you of nerves that are beneath, and the bloodletting should cross also as in cutting; and the flames should be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood does not come out, then put the foot back in the water and let the vein be completely drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the swabber fails the first time, he recommences the second above a pouch, because the place is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The lesion of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the thigh, and its bloodletting is worth for pain in the backside, when it's for hot bleeding.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his blood is such that the patient enters into water and stirs above the shin four days in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let him bleed in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and beware lest you cut too much, for the place is safe, and it has been repeated many times.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that opens at the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make such cutting of the blood as you see fit, and then release the string, and put on cotton and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bleedings from a vacuum cup
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venesections are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and venesecting is done in two ways: either by piercing and attracting blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction which is without a needle is in two ways: either it is all in flame, or almost in flame; and the suction that is made by cutting and extraction of blood is done on fourteen places of the body, where one is at the top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others are in both sides of the neck; and the suction under the chin; and the suction from the armpits; and the suckers from both arms; and the suckers from both legs; and the suckers from both ankles; and this suction does not treat with blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it has not weakened anyone at all, just as one makes a vein-opening; and it must not be administered, nor all at flame nor almost at flame, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if because of necessity of illness it becomes necessary to bleed, or for habit, so we bring them each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and in each time; for there are such that, when they need to be bled, so have a heavy head; and such who find repletion and redness on their face, and on their head, and in their neck, and darkness behind their eyes; and such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they spit out blood; and there are those who sleep, and see through their blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it's in the middle of the month, let us command them to venesect three hours after lunch.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding from the nostrils so helps with the inflammation of the head that comes to the eyes, and it does not seem right that this should happen after the evacuation of all the blood from the body; and this bleeding is in place of the bleeding from the cerebral vessel, and it does not seem right that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have catarrh, for it causes them great harm; and therefore old people do not use it, nor those with head cold illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves with this often become forgetful, and because of that it is advisable to place the venesecting a little lower down by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vapour-sation on the neck is in place of the seat of the sinew of the head and of the vertebrae, and for this it is worth it to tighten the belly and to split the channel of the womb, and for a tumour, and for repletion; and it must be pressed firmly, because if it holds too tightly, it obstructs obstipation or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vapour-sations on both sides of the neck are worth for the pains of the head, and ophthalmia, and migraine, and for choking, and for the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the seat of the vertebrae; and you must command the surgeon that he extends his hand to put, that he does not touch the artery, and does not take away too much blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venesecting below the chin is worth for diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it takes the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The venesecting of the armpits is worth for disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The vapour-sations of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they attract blood from these large veins; and command the surgeon that he does not make too great an incision in depth, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies next to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venesecting that is above the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases below it. And let the venesecting be large and made of iron, so that it can draw well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesectings of the legs are clearly curative, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains in the reins, the bladder, and the kidneys, and they calm the ulcers; and they take the place of the two saphena veins and the two ankles. And moreover, they weaken the body after long use, and cause faintness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the venesecting is that you first put it on empty and then fill it with blood, quickly attach it to the body and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pierce, and reapply the venesectings, and take note of the condition of the body, for there are some who have thick flesh and clear pores: if so, you should only prick once, and make large and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out some blood little by little, one suffices once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out much blood, so be it repeated often; and if the blood is thick, then pierce deeply, and the ends should be such that the vessels are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for one with hard skin and rough, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with dissolving oil: as in estate, with violet oil or oil of sweet almonds or oil of cucumber seed; and if it is in winter, with oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or hawthorn oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person whom one treats has tender flesh and large pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil on them, but rather they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or Morellet's water, or cucumber seed water, or porcelain water, or another similar one.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, should get up with ashes, or mulberry water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive fullness are to rise from old wine, or vinegar of wormwood, or decoction of hawthorn or chamomile, or similar things; and they do not need to be relieved by a poultice before bathing nor in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and they must not sleep afterwards, but rather take care, when it is time to apply a poultice and when they are poulliced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are sick with a choleric temperament, and whose blood is too fiery and inflamed; so it's necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the summer, and similar things; and pomegranate juice, and venison, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, so take honey syrup, and medium-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and pomegranate juice, and pomegranate juice and small birds and pigeons; and the day that they will be ventoused, so they should drink more than eat; and it's necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or musk before the ventouse or afterwards, in order to comfort the main members; but make subtle the blood, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Those which are applied with iron to strike are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips and the thigh, for those members do not tolerate being struck on them, and one does it only to attract blood from member to member, as we put on the chest when the wound is bleeding; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put ventouses on the belly and on the groin to reduce the member; and to remove the pain, where there is inflammation or a stone, it removes by its attractive virtue either the inflammation or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained wind; and such ventouses are administered empty to suck out only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot herbal tea, as in eye diseases, and in this manner one fills the ventouse with warm water alone, or with water where it has cooked herbs that are beneficial for those things.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the venesecting administered with fire is such that:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it must be two palms wide and half a palm deep, and it should be around the middle of the back about little pocket, so as to put a needle in it, and it should be made of silver; soft to the front so that it does not hurt the patient when putting on the member. And it must have a strip of crossing iron or iron in the middle, so as to put a candle inside clamped, and there should be large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the poultices of children are other than old people, and thin than fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this poultice on the member: grasp the candle with wax or the unguent and put it inside the poultice through the strip which is inside the poultice, so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice so it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and it must be above the little pocket that we have said, so that when one wants to go out, if there is vapor, take off the poultice; and grasp the unguent again as before, and repeat it often, if you need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	With the ventouse that is administered in the illness of pleurisy, at all times sharp, has no spike or point, and is not applied forceful than when it is filled with liquid, and is placed on the member so only.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Blistering is not applied forceful than in members where you cannot put ventouses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare places of flesh, such as the eye or heel, and other similar ones. And the quality of the blister ointment is that when you find blisters that are in sweet clean water with red pus, take them; and put one in sweet clean water until they are attached, and have nothing inside; and then let it be cleaned with vein and ventouse, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the blisters; and when they are full, and bursting, if that's a place where you can put a ventouse, then put one in, because that will help afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the place from oil and then from water, well, and then press it; and if the place is healed too soon after the stitches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put on it, so that the stitches are closed; and if there is a lot of bleeding, put on vitriol crushed or gallstones, and similar things, until it closes; or you put half of roasted chickpeas on the place, and leave them until they adhere to the place, which will now close; and if you need more bandages, take others.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bandages do not stick well, rub the place with fresh blood, or you insert a needle into it until the bleeding comes out, and then put on the bandages, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are leaking, sprinkle some powdered aloes and silk ashes, or charcoal, onto them now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and they bring relief from bruising and swelling.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish men stumble upon this chapter, who have never seen any of the ancient books nor read a letter about it; and for this reason is the science estranged in our land, because I found none good; and I know nothing more than by the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter those things contained, and have abbreviated them at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments brought together, as I did in these two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is necessary for us to say the prologue of this book, where are gathered the words and chapters in which the wise man puts his understanding, and stays on virtue, so that those who have experienced wisdom may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient in some way, on one hand and on the other, if nothing else works, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and use a cool diet, that is to say, cold juices, and meat of bird and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of hot abscess or spreading of matter in the member; if the patient revives to his first governing which he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to recover, it is necessary that one nourishes the sick person with foods that make large nourishing meat, or have viscosity, such as bread cooked in water, and rice, and eggs, and pieces of veal, and fish fresh and fat, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishing, the swelling decreases and the bruise recovers more quickly.
