Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old people and decrepit ones cannot be well taken back or soldered according to their nature because of the scorning of members, nor also those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset on the broken bone the thick threads which have been made hard and joined the member together, so that it strengthens itself just like it was before; and do not stop doing this work, and therefore he must be fed on thick meats, such as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that bruises are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the bruise of the head is different from the bruise of the chest, or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of bruises.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are bruises that spread outwards, and others that converge, such as the crack in a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also bruises with cuts, and bruises with a small split all at once.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind of wound it has its instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes back into its place; and the breakage of the bone is known by that the joint is twisted, and appears well from outside, and sounds with the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then it has no breakage; but it can well have twisting, or fissure, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move the member with your hand, but put on medications that come next, and then bind it now carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in a spiral, and are the two parts disjointed, it must now be put to equal points, thus as abscesses heat come; and if heat comes from an abscess, then leave alone a day, until the abscess is calmed; then place on an ointment that you can easily and safely apply, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of one with pieces; then hold fast, as it is necessary after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it stretches from two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or on your hand it is a small limb, or two tendons, or one tendon and at your hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are freed, then reunite by all means the additions in their places with the ointment you can use, and take care that through your work no injury nor pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the hand if you think that it is not well: straighten it beautifully, and do not bind it too tightly, nor press it as those who cause hot apostemes and contractions in the member, as we have said many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at rest, then chastise the patient so that it does not move, neither in sleeping nor in waking, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and see to it that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, then it is not at rest, and you must put it in such a disposition that it feels no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that there is no twisting when it is restored; and the quality of the broken member will be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: you must envelop them with soft and subtle linen drapery; and those that are large, such as thighs and shanks: you must envelop them with a wide and hard cord, for the thick cords encircle the entire large member and hold it tightly from all sides, so that there is no slackness; then tie light wraps around three or four times according to the member, and bind your hand in one end of the cord, then go above the break and bind it less tight, so that the break may move a little away from the break; and soften the cord gradually, bit by bit, until you take up most of the healthy part, then take hold of the other cord, and turn around back down on top of the broken place; then go to the part below the break, and bind it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first paragraph above; then put linen or drapery wraps between the cords until they are entirely even, then tie everything up with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is a swelling or abscess, put something soothing over it that has been warmed up, and removes the swelling, and leave it thus for some days; then bind onto the area with stars, and they should be of the width of half a thick rope or of oak wood from which we make awls, or of palm leaves, and according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the star put over the break be a little thicker and wider than the others; and also as long as it needs to be for the size of the limb small or large; then bind on the stars in the same way as you did at the first dressing, then tie above a string evenly, as was done at the first dressing above the break; the tighter the better; and it is necessary that the string be middle-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the strings are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bandages from twisted linen threads, and this is a great error, because the dressing cannot be even if they are too fine, and it should not have between each star less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the threads of the tassels after they have been tightened in their place, then put under them stitches of linen, or ragged lint, so that it doesn't bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is on top of the break and the stitches are broken, I will say the treatment for that afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind with straps all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the members are large, there is no need to put cauterizers that burn immediately after five days or seven, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring; and see here the manner of ancient ointments for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take from flour that stays at the walls of the mill, and mix with abundant egg white, and put this concoction neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many conditions, and indeed for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of an ointment restoring breaks and dislocations and torsions: take 3 parts of absinthe, lasana, henna, asafoetida, and gum arabic; myrrh and aloes, each 5 parts; aloe 9 parts; and make powder out of it, and mix it with abundant egg yolk; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this ointment, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsion: take myrrh and gum arabic, each ten drachmas; galbanum and aloes, each nine drachmas; acacia six drachmas; Armenian balsam ten drachmas, and grind well, and mix with water or abundant egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of applying a plaster to joints and bones that have become dislocated from their place, and to soothe the pain occurring; they use bone, and fracture: take new linen, and soak it in oil and cook it in lard, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore [the joint], but they are good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthy potato leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of applying a plaster to restore the breaking of the bone and to soften the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of vervain, chamomile, violet flowers, and flour of vetches, each one part; and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix with moisted water of coriander or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of applying poultice more strongly than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of verbena, and seeds of flax, weld, mallows, and plantain, and violet flowers and chamomile, all in equal part; and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it with anything more than wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between too soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, things that are dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, which we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is useful for wounds and pain: take mugwort and the tops of clover buds or goose feathers, wormwood, and equal parts of each, and grind them, and make a plaster out of it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the poultice a little later, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it hasn't loosened by hands of days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with no rest, or swelling, hurry, and loosen, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a moist seaweed sponge, and plunge into water, and lift up the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is eased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind on a nut, as long as you are sure of hot abscess; and be rid of the inflammation of the member, and the pain go away, then resume the subtle binding, and a little poultice, and don't strain it that hard as before; and do it subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the swelling is gone and redness, pain, and inflammation have all disappeared, and you need to reapply plaster and bandage, then start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the member of any of what we have said, do not untie it until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and at no time leave it 20 days, according to what one sees, as long as the swelling decreases, and approaches the skin above; then the restraint tightens more than before, and the meat thickens its flesh, just as I said beforehand; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary is, know that there will be no swelling; therefore take hot water to clean it, every time you untie it, and apply a poultice for an hour: thus the swelling is cut off from the member, and quickly cure what the foolish physician does, who leave the member twisted: this is bad, and is a fearful work, and I see nothing else but to let it out and to work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like you're changing the topic to "fractures" or "breaks" (in French: "brisure"). Would you like me to continue translating medieval medical texts on this subject?
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breaking, and various figures, and the causes are designated; for there are breaks that are caused by a blow from a sword, and the arm crushes all the bone down to the spongy part which is under the bone, as done by an axe or a club; and on account of this it is called this manner of break "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound of these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blunt strike, or a crack, or a blow from the fist of stone, or falling on stone, or other such things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches just to the tissue that is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is closed up in the bone as subtle as a hair, and it is a small crack, and on account of this it is called this break "capillary"; and if the wound which is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of the bone enter downwards, and there is a hollow like that which blacksmiths make when they beat up on the cauldrons, so that the iron enters.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in children who have moist bone, as a child's head; and it happens to all these manners of break where small pieces are separated from each other like that; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we are familiar with all the manners of fractures by observing them up close and through further investigation, and also from the corrupted flesh that is over them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is known by this: when the bone has been uncovered and one rubs it in gently, if the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be careful about the accidents of the sick person, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of mind, swelling, bruising, fever with chills, and the limbs becoming hot and red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrible accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents we have mentioned do not come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break in the bone comes just to the cloth that covers the brain, you must make a cut on the broken part thus: and take hold of the head of the patient who is hurt, and uncover it over the bone in every way that you can, and over the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and if bleeding from cutting comes out to reveal the bone, or an abscess forms, then use what is needed by this, and be sure of stopping the bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut on the narrow part in front, and this is the shape
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put .1. another splint larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various splints of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron indeed; and in working lightly, so that you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it's necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer splints with tapers, not going deep enough to penetrate beyond the bone of the breast, and there should be above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each comes back into its place on the spine of the bone, so that you have tapers for all breasts; and this is the shape of the three ways of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one taper above the bone and turn it to your hands so much as you know that the bone is pierced; then place the other end of the taper elsewhere a little bit afterwards, and do this all around, then cut with the forceps the space of the bone which is between the punctures, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so much that you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the head nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, then you must put back the fragment that remains of the bone with another instrument similar to a knife, but it should be sharper and more subtle than the other knife; and if nothing of the small bones or scales remains, gently remove them with instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of treatment that Galen says is more sure, and he highly recommends it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, in the place where the break is most open; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will put under the head of this incisional lens something like it.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut one part off, and the parts are sharp in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet upwards, so that you lightly chip the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane below; if it sticks to the bone, gently scrape it off, for it can be scraped off without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach right to the tissue, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to cover up that roughness, and remove the scales with a subtle file that you should have various quantities of, so as to smooth out each place the most convenient, according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass before great files, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate fractures and subtleties, it is necessary that you smooth out according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another double cloth of two or three thicknesses, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible so that you do not harm the abscess, then administer above another layer, and do not compress it too tightly until it only tightens the wound slightly; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the inflammation of the abscess is calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and flaxseed meal, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and administer medicines in moderation without biting; and be careful that the wound is completely clean before you leave any ointment there, nor assemble any stitches, for when stitches assemble over the brain cloth, they will run and rot, and the patient will suffer great harm; for when something biting is placed on the abscess, it corrodes above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Be careful then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil does not come to a head because of the medicine that has been put on it, so that it will have no virtue, then you should take one part of honey, and III parts of rose oil, and mix them together I drapeling, and apply it to the boil; then treat the wound in ways of treatments that are necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone is separated, because they are two bones; and that below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it does not make a great wound to bind or twist it, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should apply your little finger or a small probe to the navel, and place the break even with your middle finger, and at the back, until the navel returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and you cannot reach it with your finger, it is necessary that you put a small roll of cloth into the nostril to guide your probe.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do it in the same way, and hasten to restore the original state on the first day, if you can; and if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then apply a bandage of linen at the navel, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should insert another cloth from the other part, if the break is there; and let the tents be so big that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said a certain physician that one must moisten the tents with wax, and turn each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is well, but it should be that they are moistened with the confection of wheat flour, and egg, and miller's powder; then leave the tent until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one inserts an owl's feather into the nostril in place of the tent, and wraps a cloth around it to keep it in place, and then has the patient blow through it; do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then put ceruse or cotton soaked in rose oil or in a small amount of dragon's blood into the nostril.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if suppurating boils do not come, then apply plaster from the outside, with sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then put on light torches, and do not bind it too tightly; and if the break of the neck is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract it to suitable instruments for that; then cover the wound, and treat things growing in raw flesh, and soldering, as with plasters and ointments suitable for that; and if there is no inside the neck a wound, then treat it with tents, and I put in poultices of linen, until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the breaking of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken underneath, and there is no wound outside, and the break is only in the depth, not split into two parts, but rather bent inward, then it can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your two index fingers inside the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side of the jawbone, then put the tip of your right hand's index finger inside, and gently push the break into place with a slight pressure, and secure it from the outside with the other hand, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of three parts, as long as it remains even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the dislodging of the teeth occurs or breaking, you should stretch strings made from gold or silver or silk, then place them on the broken jawbone; and place above it one double cloth drape; and put on top of the drape a strong iron pin well-made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it in front with what you can, and order the patient to rest, and serve them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's appearance changes, you should remove it on the third day, and then re-set what has changed; and apply a poultice on top, of mill powder with abundance of egg or fine sesame flour, after you have removed the cloth wrapping; and put on top a light linen bandage, and if the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as they are healed. Often people are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess forms, then administer what we have said many times before (i.e., a poultice and rest).
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward no part of the bone is lost from it; if subtlety to extract with tools suitable for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have taken out all these pieces and there remains none, sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on one suitable ointment to prevent scab, until it be healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks many times in front of the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two parts, with pieces, and it is the most lightweight to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is thus when the break is without wound, that you have two attendants, so that one holds the assistant that feels the broken collarbone; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then place the break on your hands, so that the shape be as it should be, and there be no appearance nor swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round spear of cloth or linen, and as thick as your necessity requires; then stretch and lift the collarbone, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the break back into its proper shape.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone outwards because it goes deep, it is fitting that the patient lies on their side on a pillow, and places under their shoulder one middle-sized cushion, and pushes the attendants' shoulder down, so that the bone of the collarbone is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find it disjointed, it is fitting that you split it open; and pull out the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot join together with any adjustment, cut off one of the fragments with a pair of scissors that you have; but be sure to place under the collarbone this instrument, to protect the joint.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems a spoon, and is not shaved, and should be as wide as it fits around the bone and the power of the work; and have two sockets, as you see, and one is wide and the other narrow, just like the outline of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure there is a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the scabbing is small or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloth and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms there, moisten it with a cloth in olive oil, rosewater, and vinegar, and apply it to the skin.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster made from the powder of the mill and almond oil, and put light bandages over it, and take a spear under the strap, if you need one; then take a very long bandage of a palm in width, then put double cloth on top of the bandages and the plaster; then take a fine splint of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and put the splint over the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy joint, and under the diseased joint; and rinse each part, and when you see that the dressing holds the break securely, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, so reward it every day, and when the stitches loosen, then hold it firm; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small bolster under the joint, to lift the arm up high; so it will alleviate the breaking of the collarbone by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad occurrences come, until twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and bind and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in no more than twenty-eight days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	This appears to be a header or title for the next section of text, rather than a complete sentence. It translates to "Of the break of the shoulder".
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is broken or its place is stretched and you don't know whether it's dislocated by the touch; if it heals according to the figure of the break, and resets itself according to its natural form in every way that you can; then put on the place powdered mill with a lot of egg white, and light cloths, and put on double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle bandage, a little more wide than the shoulder, and under the bandage there are hooks in no part of the shoulder so that you sew that hair with linen threads, so that the bandage is evenly; and then hold it all with a strong band tightly, so that the bandage doesn't move from its place, and watch over the patient every day; and every time it heals, tighten, and put even the bandage if it's out of its place, and lay the patient on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be certain, for it's not bone that sets itself free lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone projects forward and points downward below the kneecap, then make an incision above it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the treatment of a hot abscess to calm it.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the breast (shoulder)
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens infrequently; however, it often breaks at its end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, then it inclines to the underside, and the patient feels great pain, and because of lack of plastering, and soon, by chance, they vomit blood, and the sinews appear in the broken bone, and it seems very bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and they place a cushion between their shoulders, then press down on their shoulders, and bring together the ribs of the two collarbones with their hands, and carefully do it in all the ways you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put salves and ointments above the broken ribcage, made from salt or another light wood, and wrap it up in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and turn the string around to the back, and hold it tightly, and every hour loosen the string a little, and if it becomes too loose, tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or itching that comes on the surface, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, and remove the ointment, and treat what has come up in ways of cures; then rinse off the ointment, and hold it tight until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	The text appears to be a medical treatise from medieval times, describing the treatment for broken ribs (costes). The translation I provided earlier attempts to convey the instructions given in the original text.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the bursting of the ribs does not occur except in thick places after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend more than because they are slippery; and people know this well at the examination on the spine.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is to place the break even, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind it with an iron band if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the bursting of the ribs is declining inside, the patient feels very great pain and puncture, as well as a tearing, for the bone pierces the flesh; and he groans with sharp pains, and is tormented with great vomiting of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancient ones have put great art into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that fill the belly, in order to push the bursting outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, so that hot abscesses do not form there, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let him be healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And one of us said that we should apply cupping glasses on the spot to draw out the pus, and this seems like reason; however, there is doubt whether the cups will attract the superfluidities to the spot because of the weakness of its location.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one of us said that we should cover the spot with a damp woolen cloth in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to put everything back in its place; then it can be treated according to the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain because of the bone that points through the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the viscera; and then you must saw the bone, and pull it out gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and cure them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, then put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil and place on the lesion; and cure the place of the abscess while it is thus, and be careful to apply a poultice to the adjacent part where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	When the fracture occurs at the neck of the bone, and it bends, and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, it does not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Understand that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they feel and move well when you restrain them and prick them, understand that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if a treatment is applied there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take note if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in the hands, and there is sweating and vomiting without will, on his back; and when he has been relieved on his belly, if there is vomiting without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he lies on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: no cure can be worked for him.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should apply if there is a hot abscess, put on top of it oil of rose or oil of egg yolk until it is calmed down; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, as long as it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bones are broken, it is necessary to cover the wound with a dressing; and remove the bone, then close the two lips of the wound together with a suture, if they are large, then anoint with ointment dripping fat as long as it heals; and if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called "the joint of the knee", take your pouch from your left hand and put it equal to the other hand in your power, then apply the plaster and the splint on top, if necessary; then bind it tight, and if there are loose bones, make them fast, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	The break of the hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	A small thing happens when the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a small decrease in strength of the head; and do not move too much, and decline to one side, and come to the patient with pain at the spot where it broke, and puncture, and inflate what was broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you stretch your hand over it, as long as you are above the break; and know what the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head alone, put it back in the same shape, so that it is in a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it bends inward, make the patient lie on their stomach, as long as you can see the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it back in place, then apply a poultice on top, and put a splint of wood or bone, and bind the break so that it does not move; and apply a cloth under the ribs, as long as the pain is equalized.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it, as long as the abscess is calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then come back to the restoration, and bind it as it should be done, if there is no bad accident; and that's how to do it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the arm (shoulder) or more specifically, the scapula (shoulder blade).
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The arm or shoulder blade is the bone between the elbow and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it should be restored in one of two ways: one way is to take a piece of wood, smooth and thicker, with this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lay the two shoulders on top of one another, and bind them together with two cords; then raise up the patient on one seat; then throw his broken arm on the shaft so that it comes to rest in a hole, and place a wooden wedge in between; then let him stretch out over any heavy object or the attendants will hold him down below; then place the splint even with his hands together, until the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to raise the patient on his hindquarters, and tie his hand behind his neck; then command two attendants that one take hold of what is above the splint with his hands, and the other take hold from below of all the straps, and each stretch it to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, restrain the piece under the breakage and above it, and stretch each of the parts to its share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breakage is near the head of the shoulder, it behooves you to put the middle strap under the arm and the other towards the armpit, under the breakage; and likewise if the breakage is toward the armpit, it is necessary to put the lighter strap lightly, without effort, until the breakage is even on the joint and on the armpit; then set the breakage even as it behooves you and bind it, lest an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if swelling comes, then do not tighten it until 7 days, and put on a linen cloth dampened in lard and rose oil, as long as the swelling is calmed; then tighten it. And the way to tighten it is that you place the splint on the splinter, then assemble the arm on the elbow rest, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and tighten on the elbow rest, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, as long as no obstacle prevents it, or if the bone has not been dislocated.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone has not been displaced, then use splints, and put on the splint a larger and stronger bandage than the others, with about two inches between each bandage, so that each bandage is as large as to pass over the splint three inches from each side; then tighten on the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the splint, tighter and less loose.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the sitting of stars and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it alone until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each III days the bandage, lest it becomes suppurated or inflamed at the place, where the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it adheres, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes to it, do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion full of wool even, and look at each hour of day or night that the shape of the broken member does not move, or be softened the ligaments; if it adheres through the virtue of medicine, and give him the food which we have mentioned before, in such a manner that the food is at the first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be readjusted in forty days from the start; and then one must loosen and administer bath and ointment medicines to set the place right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and twisted, it should remain untied for ten days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of 2 bones, which are called the "foscile", of which one is small and is located near the shoulder; and the other is large and is located under, towards the elbow joint. By chance, only the large bone breaks, or the small one, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then one should gently extend it and straighten it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is a large bone that is broken, then one should bind it more tightly; and extend it upwards on the cushion, and have the patient's arm crossed over himself, with the hand higher than the others, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch out the servants' other arm to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and another servant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put in him a mirror equal to his best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has left pieces that are not dislodged, then put each one back in its place. And if there is any part that cannot be returned to its place without touching it with an instrument, as we said before, then proceed to extract the bone, and let the fragments alone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	This text appears to be written in an archaic style of French, specifically from the 13th or 14th century. I'll translate it into modern English:
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment a hot abscess appears, apply to it a cloth made from rosie oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and tie up the cloth gently until the hot abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax and put on a poultice of flour powder with abundance of egg, then apply the stars, and let the star of the breakage be at once stronger and somewhat larger than the others; and know that it must have six stars or more in various positions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and bind more tightly above the breakage than elsewhere, and always less loosing, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the threads by which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, you should bathe the member with hot water until those itches are calmed; and let the member not tightly rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin to bind again, and if the ligament is relaxed and the bone loosened, and similar thing, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.
