Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is back in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then untie and leave it alone.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then moisten with hot water, and rub him until he is cured.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	This appears to be the title of the medical text snippet you provided, which seems to describe treatments for a dislocated joint in the hand. The text was written in Old French and may have been a medieval medical manuscript.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the bones of the hand are dislocated to each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or in the wrist; then the bone is bent and push the dislocation towards your pouches until it returns, then hold the head of the bone, and turn it towards the part where it was separated; and let it be two days, and then make it even that day; and put the splint on it, as we have said, and release it each day, and make it move, and bind it with a nut; and do this often, until it is tight, and do just so when it is dislocated to the wrist of the hand, and do thus, in case it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The Dislocation of the Hip Joint (from the back).
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip joint or joints from the back or neck are dislocated, and there is more than one dislocation, then there is no remedy, for the bone quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the evacuations jump without will, and it cannot be held, and many times a limb becomes soft, or both shoulders or two arms; and many times the hip swells to four parts; that which swells at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that if gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure nor recovery at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancient manner of cures by great words say it has no great profit at all; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have fashioned instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositez that comes to the front of the chest, there is no cure nor healing; and also that which comes directly on both sides, and one cannot treat those who come properly on the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lies stretched out on his face in a level place, and has something strained underneath him so he does not cut himself; then put two brands at the head in the earth firmly, and another at the feet, and tie one thread beside the patient's hips, and another beside the thighs, and knees, and ankles; and two servants know the threads, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two brands; and they are well tied, the brand as we have said, and the physician puts his palms on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not come back through this treatment, then take a board of three arm's length in width, and hollow under the surface, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board under the surface, then put the middle of the board over the spine; and have the sick person place their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not work, do it with a turning post which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And is that you sharpen two stakes at the head of the patient one arm's length in width, and towards the feet two others, and have between each stake, on top and underneath, a palm's breadth in length; and have on each stake one nail, or the turning post fits, and be the stakes firmly stuck in the ground so that they do not move; and between each two stakes have one turning post, around which the ligament turns, and have on the two turnings two small stakes of a palm's length, to turn the turning post; and then tie the ligament that is between the bones to the turning post towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet to the other turning post, and each of the servants turn their post until all the ligament, and the master make the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, apply a desiccating plaster with abundant egg white, and then bandage it, and then sew it with a needle of III dinars' length, which stretches the place of the elbow joint and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use gentle massage on the patient until they are healed; and if anything comes at the end of healing, administer soothing medicines and analgesics, with the needle that we mentioned before; and sometimes give them a piece of cloth, and sometimes the appearance comes in the lower part of the spine behind the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; and this is the bone which has opened up, so one should not have any presumption: perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip. (This seems to be a new section or chapter in the text)
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder are prone to dislocation alone, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated into .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and in front and behind; and more inside than that, and often dislocates before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is this: when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee opens more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee; and there is a swelling in front of the warm abscess, because the hip bone comes to that place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes out to the outside, is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it comes in front, are that they straighten well their leg according to completion; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee with pain, and if you want them to go, they cannot advance, and retain their urine, and swell the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it comes behind, are that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the blood of the thigh is at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you should return to see if the dislocation is ancient, and it remains according to its condition, then there is no cure; and it is not necessary to have any confidence in it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of three manners of dislocation, you should hasten to turn back the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not come back in this way, you must appear to the minister strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or on one ligature that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand thus so that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then tightens him with a soft ligature above the thigh; and another pins the chief of the ligature; and they all stretch upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and hangs.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to the three similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat his resemblance When the dislocation is in the parting, you must put the patient on their side sound, then place the ligature above the root of the thigh, and the place that is under the groin, then stretch the ligature upwards towards the groin, and towards the crease; then take another minister's arms, and encircle the thick part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it out to its full length: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot close it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the patient's two feet together with a strong soft cord above both heels and both knees; and let the sick leg be stretched out two fingers more than the others; then hang it from the end of a pole, and raise it six hands above the ground; then command one servant to encircle the bottom part of the loins, and have another servant hanging with the patient, who encircles them together, because the joint is now coming back hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation has come to its end, if the patient lies down, as we have said in that who had gilbositis, and loosen the cord above the sick leg properly, and on the thigh also; then put two burning brands, one at the top and the other at the feet, then stick the brand between the loins of the patient in the shape; and have moistened cloths planted around so that he does not hurt himself, then stretch out each servant towards him, and the physician sets equal to his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table, and press thus as we have said in the surgery, and place the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to extend the sick leg hastily and according to what I said; and let the surgeon put his hand above the knee of the sick person, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the ankle.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it does not seem necessary to stretch the patient downwards or lift him up on the earth, but rather that he should be as if his hip were dislocated on the outside, as we have said about lying on two hips; and let him be on his face, and the bandage stretched as we have said before, and it must press on the joint at the table; and it will be in place when the patient stretches out his legs and they will be equal; then join the thighs, and apply the splint, and strain from a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and if he rests for three days or four, then loosen it, and put the splint on him; and if you see that they are equal, tie the strain as before, and let him rest for three days; then loosen it, and make him walk slowly, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated according to three manners: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and do not come loose in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at his knee, and if it does not bend at his knee, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your arms, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant extends his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it bends well at the knee lightly; and apply the poultice above, and make the leg stable at the knee, and keep them together tightly for three days or four, then release him; and do not let the patient work, until the limb is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not in place, then administer strong extension, just as we have said in the treatment of the shoulder, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	This appears to be a new topic. The phrase "de la dislocation dou talon" roughly translates to "of the dislocation of the heel". Would you like me to help with that?
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	This text appears to be discussing the anatomy and movement of the foot, specifically the heel.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the joint is swollen, and stretch before to the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and it must be extended lightly with the hands when it is felt only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated to its entirety, then you must make the patient sit upright, and place the instruments apart by the leg, above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand, and then in your left twice, then stretch it up high, and push the foot up well; and do this twice, just as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot come back so, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a firm beam in the earth between his thighs, and tie cloths around him, so he does not injure the patient; then another minister places the leg, and another minister stretches the foot out with their hands or with a strap, to which they tie it above the ankle of the foot; then each minister stretches equally, and the beam is thus between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when you stretch it; then place one minister equally on the dislocation in his hand, and another minister places the healthy leg under him, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is well-shaped, then apply the poultice and cloth on top, and strain to hold firm, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch that the bandage is not too tight; then let him be for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, reapply it; then unbind on the fourth day or quarter, and keep the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before this term is over, it is by no means certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a swelling comes on the place, you should apply what we said to calm it down, until he is completely healed.
des dois	It looks like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! Thank you for translating and sharing it with me. It's fascinating to see how medical practices were described in old texts, even if they might not be entirely effective or safe by modern standards.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the knees are no longer dislocated, you should have them stretched out nicely without effort, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in some other part of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot over the parts of the joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even and there is no protrusion, place under the sole of the foot a table two feet long, then bind firmly, and let him be for three days, then unbind him; and have him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	a wound and a dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at the beginning things calming abscess hot, and let the patient be in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the member to its place, so that the hot abscess comes; and when the member is at its place, then administer things calming abscess hot, and treat the wound, as it is necessary, with ointments drying out; and if with dislocation there is fracture, and small bones separated, break them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge that arms and saves your body.
